each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都帶著它的負120個訊息 , 它會旋轉 , 如果它到達那裡 , 然後傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 研究這個計畫 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為這真的會帶來光:這真的很可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美金 , 許多人花時間來製作這八英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能擴大它嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人嵌入每個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 , 看看被動的大自然 , 或被動地嘗試重新設計程式 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 它嘗試進行實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上嵌入了最基本的計算元件 , 數位邏輯大門 , 直接進入你的零件 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是一個nand大門 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	有一個四面體 , 它會做你的計算 , 另外有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是用戶的輸入 , 當你在建造你的磚塊時 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一個則是從前一塊磚塊被放在那裡 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	接著 , 它會讓你在3d空間中產生輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始加入他們想要的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它之前的做法 , 以及你說你想要做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 向上或下移動 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , 輸入等於0輸出 , 輸出就會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 輸入是1個輸出 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的東西的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有資訊嵌入其中 , 內容是建構出來的 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱之為自動化複製 , 因為你的結構包含了精確的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都嵌入來告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有一些可以攀爬的東西 , 把它讀出來 , 可以在一個人身上輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個專案叫做 「 偏見鏈 」 , 它可能是我們現在最令人振奮的自我組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以需要重新設計和程式設計 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都完全相同 , 它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每一鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要向右轉或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以 , 當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上是在編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你要告訴每個單位是否應該轉向右或左 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈 , 它就會折疊成任何你編寫的配置 , 以此為例 , 螺旋 , 或這個例子 , 兩個立方體相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以編寫任何三維形狀或單一的二維形狀 , 完全被動化到這個鏈中 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來的什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為它告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復、建築物、機器有新的可能性 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的程式性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那你有新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都能計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是很棒的平行和分散式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這很讓人興奮 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為 , 我在這裡展示的這些專案只是未來的一小步 , 如果我們為新自我組合的世界實現這些新技術 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 我們繪製了大陸 , 我們甚至去過了海底最深的一點 。 下一代的剩下什麼 ? 生物學家和探索者納森•沃爾夫提出了這個答案:幾乎所有事情 。 我們都可以開始 , 他說 , 儘管世界上的極小 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、科學、科學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃夫:剩下什麼要去探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我拜訪了威斯康辛州的貝地 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮幸一個20世紀的探險家roychpmanandrews 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館的那段期間 , 安德魯斯帶領一系列的探險到未知的區域 , 就像在gobi沙漠這裡 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來他說 , 印第安第娜瓊斯角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特 , 我給了一群中學學生的公眾演講 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡要告訴各位 , 如果ted的演講比這裡更嚇人的話 , 它會試著把一群12歲的孩子的注意力放在45分鐘的講座上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	講座結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時起 , 有一個真的困住了我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了問題: 「 我們該去哪裡去探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想我們當中許多人認為地球上的探索時代已經結束了 , 下一代他們必須去外太空或深海尋找重要的事物 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是事實嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	到底有沒有什麼重要的意義可以讓我們在地球上探索剩下的 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回想了生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是一個探索未知世界的探險家 , 馬丁usbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	北京人開始發現菸草的致命原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是把被感染的果汁從菸草植物中過濾掉 , 他會透過更小的過濾器來過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到達了他覺得那裡一定有一些比我們所知的最小型的細菌更小的東西 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他想出了一個名字給他的神秘代理人 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭開病毒時 , beijerinck真的為我們開啟了整個新世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒是地球上大部分的基因信息 , 超過所有其他形式的生命的基因資訊結合 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 和這個世界有很大的實際應用 , 像是天花的消滅 , 對於天花疫苗的出現 , 我們現在知道大部分是由人類乳癌所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , 北京人發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有了汽車 , 但我們卻沒有意識到製造地球上大部分基因信息的生物形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些驚人的工具可以讓我們探索未知的世界 , 例如深度定序 , 讓我們不僅僅只是滑雪表面 , 觀察不同物種的個別基因組 , 而是去看完整的新陳代謝物 , 包括我們周圍的微生物群落 , 記錄這些生物的所有基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用到土壤、皮膚等等 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在在一個常規的基礎上做這件事 , 來辨識出疫情的成因 , 正是造成疫情的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像我們從你們的每一個人身上抽出一把nasalb的腫塊 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們通常會去尋找呼吸道病毒 , 比如流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到的是大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究遺傳信息 , 我們會看到很多人類基因信息 , 當然 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分是從你鼻子裡完全沒有任何傷害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到非常非常非常非常驚人的東西 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現在鼻子裡大約有20%的基因信息不會符合我們之前見過的任何東西 , 沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒、細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們完全不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對我們這些真正研究這種資料的小群體而言 , 我們當中的一些人已經開始稱之為 「 生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前見過的 ; 相當於我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你的鼻子裡有百分之二十的基因信息是很多的生物暗物質 , 如果我們看看你的腸子 , 高達百分之四十或五十的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對無菌的血液中 , 大約1%到2%的信息是暗物質無法被分類、輸入或配對任何我們見過的東西 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這可能是人造物 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得越來越精確 , 我們已經確定這些資訊是生命的一種形式 , 至少有些是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然 , 解釋生物暗物質存在的假設其實只是它們的嬰兒的嬰兒 , 有一個非常非常令人振奮的可能性存在:在這個遺傳信息中 , 埋藏在生命的特徵中 , 是未知的生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索a、t、c、g的這些弦時 , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生命類型 , 例如beijerinck , 將徹底改變我們對生物學的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	或許這會讓我們辨識出我們害怕的癌症成因 , 或是辨識出我們不熟悉的疫情來源 , 或是創造出分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興向大家宣佈 , 和史丹佛大學加州理工學院的同事及加州理工和加州理工學院 , 目前我們開始了一個計畫 , 來探索生命的新形式 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百多年前 , 人們不知道病毒是什麼形式 , 構成我們星球上大部分的遺傳信息 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能很驚訝 , 我們可能完全沒有意識到新的生命類型 , 其實就在我們的鼻子裡 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	的確 , 我們可能已經把地球上所有的大陸都歸納出來 , 我們可能已經發現所有外面的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他為下一代的探險家提供了很重要的一課 , 比如來自威斯康辛的小女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想 , 如果我們說出那堂課 , 就會像這樣:不要假設我們目前認為的全部故事是完整的 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	不論你選擇去探索的領域 , 都會追溯黑暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們周圍都有未知的現象 , 等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家大衛•狄塞奇把理論物理放在背面 , 討論更緊急的問題:人類的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、文化、文化、環境、環境、物理、物理、科學、科學、科技、科技、宇宙、
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛在我們宇宙中的位置 , 大衛魔鬼就在宇宙中的位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出肢體 , 說些令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這麼做 , 但我想從大家早就知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	事實上 , 首先 , 大部分記錄下來的歷史都是已知的 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 獨一無二的適應 , 維持我們的進化 , 或創造 , 如過去思索和現存 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這個想法是 , 在太空船外面 , 宇宙是無可避免的 , 裡面就是我們所擁有的 , 我們只仰賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只得到一個機會:如果我們搞砸了太空船 , 我們還有其他地方要去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二個大家都知道的 , 與大部分人類歷史所相信的相反 , 人類並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	如同史蒂芬霍金所說的 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面上的化學污霧 , 繞著典型的星球繞著一個典型的星球 , 正是典型銀河系的外層 , 等等 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 大家都知道的兩件事是說我們處一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的合適之處 , 第二個是說我們處一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是當你把這兩種深層的真相視為是為了讓你的人生決策 , 那麼他們似乎會彼此衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我從第二個開始:典型的 。 嗯 , 這是一個典型的地方嗎 ? 讓我們看看四周 , 看看隨機方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學汙染 , 完全不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所要做的只是向同樣的方向邁進幾百英哩 , 回頭看 , 你看不到任何牆或化學污垢 , 都是藍色的星球 。 如果你更進一步看 , 太陽、太陽系 , 和恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星在星系裡 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 一個典型的地方 , 幾乎沒有任何星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 讓我們再往外走 , 直到我們在銀河之外 , 回頭看 , 是的 , 有一個巨大的星系 , 上面有螺旋手臂在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時此刻 , 我們已經有十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但是我們仍然不在宇宙中典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到一個典型的地方 , 你必須走一千倍的距離進入星際空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中的典型地方是什麼樣子的 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 大量的開支 , ted已經安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 呈現出在銀河空間中看得到的銀河空間 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能否讓燈亮起來 , 這樣我們就能看到它嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不是很完美你可以看到在星系間的星系空間裡完全是黑暗的 , 音高漆黑 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	這真是太黑暗了 , 如果你看最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星被爆炸為超新星 , 而當你的光線接近你時 , 你仍然無法直接看到它 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙的大小和暗度 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星這麼亮 , 所以很聰明 , 它會在數光年間殺死你 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星際空間 , 到目前為止 , 你甚至不會看到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	外面也很冷 , 絕對零度只有三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	這是非常空的 。 真空氣的密度比地球上最高的科技還要少一百萬倍 , 目前我們最好的科技可以創造出來的 。 所以這就是典型的地方 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方是如此的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	請把燈打回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在我們怎麼知道一個遙遠遙遠的環境 , 這麼不同 , 外星人 , 從任何我們習慣的環境中 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球是我們的環境 , 以我們所創造的知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這意味著什麼呢 ? 看看比我們剛剛說的更遠的地方 , 用望遠鏡 , 看看看起來像恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們叫做 「 四軸 」 。 原本代表 「 量子星 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	意思就是 , 看起來有點像恆星 。 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道數十億年前 , 數十億光年之久 , 星系中心的物質倒塌成超大質量黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後密集的磁場會導致重力崩塌的能量 。 有些物質 , 形成了巨大的噴射器 , 光照亮了額外的亮度 , 我認為它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學幾乎不會更像這樣的噴射機的物理學 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法在它的瞬間存活 。 語言破壞了 , 當試圖描述其中一個噴射機時 , 它會是什麼樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這會有點像是經歷超新星爆炸 , 但同時也發生了數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那個噴射機在幾十億年後發生 , 在宇宙的另一邊 , 有些化學污垢可以精確描述 , 模型 , 和預測 , 最重要的是 , 這裡發生的一切 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 有一個精確的模型 , 位於四軸 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不只是一個超級富有的圖像 , 雖然它包含了它 , 一種解釋性模型 , 包含了相同的數學關係 , 以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這才是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 信心和另一個結構會隨著時間增加 。 那就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有特殊特徵 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體的物品 , 儘管它們可能是不相似的 , 仍然可以體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨時間而來 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	我們是不同的化學成分 , 這種化學成分具有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含著越來越精確的位置 。 這個位置 , 而不是宇宙中的其他位置 , 是一個樞紐 , 它本身的結構和因果本質 , 包含了整個實體現實 。 所以 , 遠不被分配 , 物理定律允許 , 甚至強迫它發生了 , 最重要的事情之一是物理世界 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	太陽系和我們的環境是如何在我們和其他宇宙的特殊關係中取得這種特殊的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 史蒂芬•霍金的標誌是正確的 , 但這是錯誤的重點 。 一件事是 , 它沒有任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有奇蹟 。 它是有三個我們在這裡所擁有的東西 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一項是很重要的 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理 。 資訊處理是一種計算 , 計算需要一個電腦 , 不知所知地製造一個電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體對我們所發現的知識產生影響 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 比較不具體 , 但對於開放式知識、解釋的開放創造 , 都是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境受到證據的影響 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	例如 , 牛頓重力定律約300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但我們過去所做的證據是在地球上數十億年前的每平方公尺下降 , 並且在數十億年後繼續下降 。 其他的科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發現所有科學中最基本的真理 , 只是為了實現我們的星球 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點充滿了證據 , 還有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三個開放式知識的前提都在它們最低的可能供給量 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說的 , 它是空的 ; 它很冷 , 那裡是黑暗 , 還是 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	實際上 , 這只是另一個假釋誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為 , 想像一個立方體存在於星系空間中 , 和我們的家一樣 , 太陽系 。 現在這個立方體是非常空的 , 但這仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸的數量足以完成 , 比如說 , 一個自我控制的太空站 , 在那裡有一群科學家 , 投入創造一個開放式的知識流 , 等等 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 除了現在的科技之外 , 甚至從星際空間收集氫氣 , 將它變成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但問題是 , 在一個可以理解的宇宙中 , 如果物理定律沒有被禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼可能阻止我們做這件事 , 除了知道如何 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動產生能量供應 , 因為轉變會是個核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	再一次 , 它是人類感官的黑暗 。 但你只需要用望遠鏡 , 甚至是現今的設計 , 看看外面 , 你就會看到我們從這裡看到的相同的星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 就能看見星星和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在這些星系中 , 你可以做天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在當地 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最困難的科學可能是生物學領域的旅程 , 因為要花數億年才能到最近的生命體 , 回到最近的星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我必須告訴各位 , 理查德 , 但我從來不喜歡生物學領域的旅程 , 我想我們能每隔幾億年完成一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	事實上 , 星系間的空間包含了所有開放式的知識 。 任何一個立方體 , 宇宙的任何一個角落 , 都可能變成相同的樞紐 , 如果我們知道該怎麼做 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不處在一個獨一無二的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系空間能夠創造出一個開放式的解釋流 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境 。 所以這是地球 。 所以這是一個污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而有限的因素 , 在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為它們很豐富 , 但知識 , 很稀有 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種以宇宙為基礎的知識觀點 , 我認為應該讓我們感受到非常特別 。 但這也應該讓我們覺得脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有特定的知識需要存活宇宙的挑戰 , 我們就不會存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一顆超新星才能離開幾光年 , 我們都會死去 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁•雷斯最近寫了一本關於我們對各種事物的脆弱的書 , 從天體物理 , 到科學實驗都出了問題 , 最重要的是用大規模毀滅的武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有百分之五十的機會能存活下來 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚點要談談這個會議 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的分類來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他這件事 , 我們可以存活下來 , 我們也無法存活下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它不依賴機會 , 而是我們是否會創造相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	這種危險完全不是前所未有的 。 物種總是滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終止了 。 絕大多數的物種和所有已存在的文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想要成為例外 , 那麼邏輯上 , 我們唯一的希望就是用一種特徵來區別我們的物種 , 和我們的文明 , 即便是 , 我們和物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造出新的解釋 , 新的知識 , 成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	讓我把它應用在當前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想要倡導任何特定的解決方案 , 只為了說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是對的物理學家 。 在全球暖化的方面 , 我只是一名懶人 。 而理性的事情是認真考慮前的科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太晚了 , 無法避免一個災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們現在最好的選擇是阻止二氧化碳排放 , 例如京都協定 , 其經濟活動的限制 , 以及數百億美金的費用 , 那就已經是任何合理的測量 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導者的行動 , 甚至還沒被求助來解決這個問題 , 僅僅只是稍微一下 。 所以這已經太晚了 , 無法避免這個問題 , 之後可能已經太晚了 , 無法避免這個問題 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代可能已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放即將降低數十億人死亡的新冰河時代 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	對於我來說 , 這一課似乎很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼沒有公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	我們不能永遠知道 。 當我們知道即將發生災難的代價 , 以及如何在災難本身成本低於災難本身的代價 , 那麼真的不會有太多的爭論 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 可以避免我們還沒預料到的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個固定的問題 , 不只是問題性 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	沒錯 , 一堆預防等於一磅的解藥 , 但只有在我們知道如何預防 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你被困在鼻子上 , 那麼醫學的科學並不包含教你如何避免穿刺 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學停止尋求治療 , 只專注於預防 , 那它也不會成功 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前世界正在燃燒計畫 , 迫使氣體排放任何成本都要降低 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要用計劃來減少溫度 , 用計劃來維持更高的溫度 , 而不是全部的成本 , 而是有效率且便宜的 。 有些計劃存在 , 例如在太空中的鏡子 , 來扭轉太陽光 , 並且鼓勵水生的有機體去吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西正在激起研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們不是人類努力去面對這個問題的核心 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們還沒意識到問題 , 要解決的能力不是無限的好運氣 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是為了生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	以兩塊石桌為例 , 然後雕刻它們 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個 , 卡維爾: 「 問題是難解的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另外一則是: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果它被困在一個不好的規則系統中 , 一個掙扎的國家要如何破除貧窮 ? 經濟學家保羅•羅默揭開了一個大膽的概念: 「 城市 」 、 「 城市 」 、 「 城市 」 、 「 城市 」 、 「 城市 」 、 「 城市 」 、 「 、 「 城市 」 、 「 城市 」 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅羅•羅默的激進點子:查爾斯的城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生正在做功課 , 在首都機場的街燈下 , 因為他們家裡沒有電力 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我見過像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子 , 綠色襯衫裡的那個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭nelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼nelson可以接觸到最先進的技術 , 像是手機 , 但無法取得一百歲的技術 , 來在家裡發電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡而言之 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以防止這種雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們可以帶來新的科技 , 讓它們成為像尼爾森這樣的人 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個規則下運作 , 說它必須以非常低、很低的補貼價格來銷售電力 , 事實上 , 它的價格非常低 , 每賣的單位都要價格 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它沒有資源 , 也沒有動機 , 要補充許多其他使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他見識到有不同的規則 , 企業賺得很小的利潤 , 所以他們有動機去簽更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	那是尼爾森的手機公司購買了他的電信公司的那種規則 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過這些規則是如何運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變電力價格的規則 , 但他遇到了來自企業和消費者的抗議活動 , 他們想要保存現有的補貼率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	他被卡住了規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏的解決方案能幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	nelson被困在街燈下 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是要試著找出我們要如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有一些規則可以發展改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想要說 , 有一個普遍的抽象觀點 , 是我們能實踐的 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給更多人更多選擇 , 在許多國家的領導者 , 更多的選擇 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但這兩者之間的反對是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能會想要給領導者這種選擇 , 像是給予總統在電力上提高價格的選擇 , 奪走經濟想要的一個選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們想要選擇繼續消耗補貼式電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到更多的選擇 , 那就給我們一套改變規則 , 來讓我們脫離陷阱的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	nelson也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想要看到規則的破壞效應 , 規則會讓人們在黑暗中保持人 , 看看美國太空總署的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是在亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 可以看到北韓 , 線上就像是鄰居的黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則讓人們處於黑暗之中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 很重要的是 , 北韓和南韓開始有相同的規則 , 在法律和法規中 , 也有更深層的了解、規範、文化、價值觀和信仰 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開後 , 他們做出選擇 , 導致了非常多樣化的道路 , 導致了他們的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變我們身為人類可以改變我們使用的規則 , 改變我們彼此互動的規則 , 更好 , 更糟的是 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	拉近海地 , 這裡是線上 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 和它的鄰居相比 , 多明尼加共和國有相同數量的居民 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這些國家的黑暗與波多黎各相比 , 有一半的居民是海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則可能是壞事 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是規則很糟 , 因為政府太強大、太壓迫 , 和北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想用良好的規則來創造環境 , 我們就不能把環境撕下來 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到建設的方法 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國大幅展現出與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這張圖表的最初 , 中國是世界高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國的先驅技術如鋼鐵、印刷、槍械 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則 , 來鼓勵這些想法的散播 , 能鼓勵傳播出去 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了一些規則 , 減緩了創新 , 把中國從世界各地砍掉 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界上其他國家創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 同時也發展出新的規則 , 中國的規則從這些進步中切斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入持續停滯不前 , 世界各地都放大了 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它繪製了美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50和60年代 , 你們可以看到 , 大約佔了百分之三 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代末期 , 發生了改變 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的經濟成長迅速趕上美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你晚上回到地圖上 , 你可以得到一個線索 , 來引導中國的戲劇變革 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最明亮的地點 , 你們可以看到在線上最亮的地方 , 是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀 , 大部分的中國的規則下 , 比起當時的其他國家 , 中國的經濟規則 , 都是由英國所統治的 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個有數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸開始 , 像縫衣服 , 製作玩具的地方 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了取得越來越多收入的過程 , 增加技能 , 導致非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是一種模式 , 像優秀xiaing可以複製 , 當他們決定把所有的大陸搬到市場模式上 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但歌唱會直覺地了解給他的人民提供選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其要求在中國的每個人立即轉移到市場模式 , 他們建立了一些特殊的區域 , 在某種意義上 , 英國的做法是:讓這個機會與市場規則立即合作 , 提供給想參與的人 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港附近建立了四個特殊的經濟區:中國可以來和工作的地方 , 都市成長得非常迅速 ; 外國公司也能進來 , 製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區塊有個叫做雪梨的城市 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市 , 有一間台iphone公司 , 讓許多人都擁有的iphone , 他們用中國的勞工來製作 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特殊區域之後 , 有14個海岸線在同樣的意義上開放 , 最終在這些地方的成功 , 讓人們可以選擇 , 因他們提供的利益而被封鎖 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證實了成功 , 導致了整個經濟模式的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一是:為人們保存選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:正確的比例 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村落的規則 , 你可以這樣做 , 但村落會太小 , 如果你有數百萬人在好的規則下工作 , 你就能得到的益處 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你就不能給人們一個機會 , 看看事情是怎麼發生的 , 然後讓其他的規則向前放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你機會創造新的地方 , 有新的規則 , 讓人們可以選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們足夠大到可以取得所有利益 , 當我們數百萬人在優良的規則下一起工作 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提議是我們構想出一個叫做 「 特許城市 」 的東西 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則開始 , 來吸引我們建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 建立基礎設施系統、道路、港口、機場、建築 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 他們會僱用先搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭 , 那些會來到那裡的居民 , 永久地養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了這篇章 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造出來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一次又一次的做 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些都被記錄在圖表裡 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模型中 , 如果我們允許建造無人居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未居住的領域開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以生活在新的憲章之下 , 但沒有人會被迫住在它之下 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是對領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要領導者的那種選擇 , 我們需要讓國家之間的合作潛力:國家合作的可能性 , 實際上 , 中國和英國的合作方式 , 首先建立市場模式 , 然後擴展到全中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國不經意地透過香港的行動 , 降低世界貧窮 , 比上個世紀所缺乏的援助計畫還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們允許這種合作 , 再複製這一點 , 我們就能讓這些益處擴展到全世界 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到責任 , 一個國家的控制權 , 從一個國家 , 到另一個國家 , 來接管某些行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這麼說的時候 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這是否會帶回殖民主義 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	這不是 。 但很重要的是 , 當我們開始思考這些事情時 , 會有這種情緒出現 , 可以讓我們退出 , 可以關掉我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索的新點子 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義的不好處在於 , 在一些援助計畫中 , 它牽涉到強制和自主權的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇 , 無論是對領導者 , 對於住在這些新地方的人 , 都有關選擇 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是對強迫和自主權的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談這如何在實踐中展現出來 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們拿一個特定的領導人雷爾卡斯特 , 他是古巴的領導人 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定有機會為古巴做些什麼 , 但他在古巴島沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他在南方有一點點光 , 有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	那裡有一個區域 , 位在瓜地馬灣附近 , 在那裡 , 一塊美國政府為一塊土地負責 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯tro去加拿大總理 , 說: 「 看吧 , 雅基斯有一個很糟糕的pr問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不去加拿大 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新的城市在那裡建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們在附近有個香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那座城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會回來 。 但這會是將現代經濟和現代世界連結起來的通道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模型還能在哪裡試驗 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 , 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	其中許多人完全得到了一種特殊區域的概念 , 讓人們可以當作一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是一種改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新的規則 , 讓人們不用強迫 , 並且反對強迫他們 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解到 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以做出更可信的承諾 , 給長期投資者 , 來建造港口、建造道路 , 在新城市裡 , 他們可以做出更有價值的承諾 , 如果他們與另一方國家合作 , 就能做出更有價值的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	甚至在某些安排中 , 有點像是一個偷竊帳戶 , 你把土地放進人群裡 , 另一方國家為此負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲也有許多土地可以建造新的城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我沿著海岸飛行的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這片土地上有巨大的延伸土地 , 在那裡 , 數億人能活下來 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們將它歸納並不僅僅是一或二個章節 , 而是數十個城市 , 能為數十億的城市創造空間 , 也許數十億人會搬到未來的城市 , 是否有足夠的土地給他們 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在世界各地 , 如果我們在晚上看到燈光 , 誤導的一件事是 , 視覺上 , 它看起來已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我告訴你們為什麼會錯 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以所有土地的代表為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個正方形 , 代表著地球上所有可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已有三十億人口居住在城市的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到矩形的底部你可以看到現有30億個城市只佔地球上30億個耕地的百分之三
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以 , 如果我們想要為其他十億人建造城市 , 他們就會變成這樣 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從三分之三的耕地 , 到百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大幅減少地球上的足跡 , 藉由建造更多人們可以搬到的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被良好的規則管理 , 他們可以是城市 , 人們安全地從犯罪、疾病、衛生、公共衛生 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	它們能得到像電力這樣的基本設備 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要怎麼開始建造第一座圖表城市 , 這樣我們才能建造更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	可以幫忙做手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做的是寫一些細節 , 可以進入這個手冊中 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們跑出城市 , 去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者在野外走出來 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們開始思考像這樣的問題 , 假設這不只是加拿大對付雷爾卡斯特的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西也有參與者 , 西班牙人 , 或許古巴也想要成為四條通路的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫出條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	之前的情況比較少 , 但這很容易就解決了 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助它 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現新加坡和香港是城市 , 讓它們在他們開始時所擁有的土地價值很大 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的價值 , 來支付像警察、法庭 , 但學校和醫療保健系統 , 讓這塊土地更吸引人居住 , 讓人們有較高的收入 , 順帶一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 協助建造這個區域的人的動機 , 設立基礎的規則 , 向正確的方向邁進 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多其他的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何有低成本且負擔得起的建築 , 像iphone , 讓這些建築物更有效率 , 確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會落在地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節要被找出來 , 但我們這些已經開始追求這些事情的人已經知道沒有路障 , 除了想像之外 , 還沒有阻礙 , 這將讓我們無法實現真正的全球雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我總結一下這張照片 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能如此順利 , 即使地球上有很多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現他們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物品 , 在那裡 , 分享意味著我們每種物品都比較少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們這樣思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:規則規則我們彼此互動的規則 , 例如 , 讓我們有一個稅收系統 , 支持研究大學 , 讓某些知識自由 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們建立一個系統 , 在那裡 , 我們有一塊土地 , 在政府辦公室裡 , 人們可以把土地保留成殖民地 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能在規則的空間中不斷創新 , 尤其是創新 , 想出改變規則的規則 , 這樣我們就不會陷入不好的規則 , 那麼我們才能繼續前進 , 真正讓世界變得更美好 , 像尼爾森和他的朋友 , 不用再研究任何路燈 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因先驅克萊格•凡特在史詩般的探險中休息 , 談到他的團隊發現的數百萬個基因 , 到目前為止 , 地圖海洋生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特在dna和海上 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我關於老化辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我明白樂觀主義者大大勝過悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我十八分鐘內 , 我會告訴各位 , 我們要如何從閱讀基因編碼 , 轉變成我們自己編碼的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅在十年前 , 我們發表了第一個免疫有機體的序列 , 也就是大氣流感病毒的第一個序列 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫從13年降到4個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以用兩到八個小時的基因組計劃來做同樣的事 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以 , 在過去十年 , 大量的基因組被加上:大部分的人類病原體 , 幾種植物 , 幾種昆蟲和哺乳類 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十多年前的思想基因組學在今年底 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組序列 ; 它的順序是數百 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂摩爾基金會得到獎金 , 到今年的130個基因組 , 作為環保有機體的一邊計畫 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀遺傳密碼的速度改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外面的狀況 , 我們幾乎沒有抓到地球上可用的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分的人不會意識到 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔地球生物量的一半 , 而所有動物只佔所有生物量的一分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	或許牛津的人們不常常這麼做 , 但如果你把它送到海裡 , 吞下一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的細菌大約有一千萬種病毒的數量 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	兩年前 , 不到五千種微生物種類的特徵 , 所以我們決定為它做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了srcerii探險 , 我們在海洋學的大探險 , 試圖將海洋樣本樣本 , 每200英里 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從bermuda做實驗 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 美國東岸 , 加勒比海、加勒比海、巴拿馬運河 , 到加拉巴哥群島 , 到太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫跨印度洋 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這很困難 ; 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 有一部分是幫助年輕人進入科學 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只用海水過濾 , 收集不同濾鏡的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們可以每24小時定序一億個基因密碼 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉由這樣做 , 我們發現了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 被認為在我們的眼睛裡的視覺色素只有一兩種有著同樣的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有在世界上溫暖的海洋中的生物都有相同的攝影器 , 把陽光當作它們的能量和溝通來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了一百三十萬個新基因 , 以及大約五萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經將它延伸到空氣中 , 帶有來自斯隆基金會的獎金 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量我們所有人每天呼吸著多少種病毒和細菌 , 特別是在飛機或關閉聽覺器 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的裝備過濾 ; 我們只收集了一億微生物的順序 , 從紐約市的一棟大樓上過濾 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們正處於定序的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	只是在資料收集的一邊 , 我們在加拉帕戈戈斯的位置 , 我們發現幾乎每兩百英里的樣本 , 我們會看到非常多樣化的樣本 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些是合理的 , 以不同溫度的角度來說 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這張照片是以溫度為基礎的衛星溫度為基礎 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣本和冷水樣本之間有很大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件讓我們驚訝的事是這些攝影器能偵測不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的胺基酸序列來預測它 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些從區域到區域各地都不相同 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外地 , 在深海裡 , 最藍色的地方 , 攝影器通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當有很多葉綠色的環狀物時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們會更加改變 , 可能在極端的紅外線和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了找出我們的基因複製品的評估 , 我們組成了所有資料 , 包括我們遠離探勘的所有基因 , 這代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 總共有大約29百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些基因家庭放入觀察這些發現:我們發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但每個我們在環境中的樣本都加上一條線性的樣本 , 給這些新家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	我們正處於地球上最早期的基礎基因、元件和生命的階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看著所謂的演化樹 , 我們和動物的右上角 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	其中大約有2900萬個基因 , 我們的基因組只有2萬4千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物集合起來 , 我們大概有不到三萬個 , 也許有十幾個以上不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因現在不僅是演化的設計元件 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 在一般的觀點上 , 或許回到理查德•達金斯的觀點 , 比起基因組成的觀點 , 這和這些基因組成的不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 已經改變了dna定序的速度 , 在過去的十年或二十年間 , 已經變得非常快速且非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組學在1995年我們將第二種基因組定序 , 從菌群的生殖器 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	大滅絕有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們簡單地問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另外500 , 有一組小型的基因可以組成一個最小的操作系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始進行轉錄突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	交通工具只是基因編碼中隨機插入的dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果它們在基因的中間插入 , 它們會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張可以接受轉換插入的所有基因的地圖 , 我們稱之為 「 不必要的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常重要 , 你只能定義一個必要或無必要的基因 , 基於環境的基礎 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智力方法和13種相關的生物體基因組進行比較 , 我們試著比較所有這些基因 , 看看它們有什麼共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們把這些重疊的圓圈找到了173個基因對所有13個有機體而言
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一個細胞寄生蟲 , 它會擴展到大約310年左右的核心基因 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 取決於你這裡的觀點 , 到大約500到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些點子的唯一方法是建造一個人造染色體 , 用這些基因組建造 , 而我們必須用一個基礎的時尚來做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 將精確的dna合成非常困難的dna 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hmsmith和clydehutchison , 我的同事們開發了一種令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能夠合成五千個鹼基的病毒 , 只在兩週期間 , 只有百分之百正確 , 以它的序列和它的生物學為基礎 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個非常令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始啟動病毒粒子的生產 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒 , 一個小兒麻痺病毒在一年前就被製造出來 , 但它只活了一千分之一 , 而且花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phhix174的漫畫 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體現在建造它自己的硬體的例子 , 這就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立刻開始關心生物戰事 , 我最近在參議院委員會的證詞 , 以及美國政府設立的特殊委員會 , 來審視這個領域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要讓現實保持在心中 , 與人們的想像力是很重要的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何現今已經被定序的病毒 , 基因組就可以完成 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上對伊波拉或天花的事物感到驚訝 , 但這種生物的dna並沒有傳染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做出天花基因組 , dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正讓人擔憂的是安全部門是設計師的病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 試圖創造出生物戰爭的代理 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這項研究真的是不完整的 , 應該要有非常少的活動才能在未來做出設計的病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞生物在兩年內是有可能的 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	而我們這些細胞 , 可能在十年內就有可能發生 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	我們現在製造了數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變這個人造染色體的類型和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 你要如何把所有的東西都放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個同質的重組系統 , 將它們重新組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體中衍生出來的無線電輻射 , 可以承受三百萬的輻射 , 而不是被殺 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發後 , 它會重新組合它的基因組 , 大約12到24小時 , 在它的染色體被爆炸後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 也許現在存在於外太空 , 是因為我們在那裡的旅程 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一個玻璃賭場 , 經過大約50萬個放射線之後 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 而微生物就在底部 , 開始變得更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這張實際的照片是這樣的:這張圖表顯示了170萬隻輻射之後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體分開了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真正令人驚訝的是這些生物能做到這一點 , 我們可能有成千上萬種不同的物種 , 能夠做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 還為了環保和社會問題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 第三種生物序列 , 甲烷含有它生活在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 其碳來自於環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 現在有數以千計的生物 , 能從二氧化碳中存活下來 , 捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其用石油來處理合成的過程 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 從大氣中捕捉它 , 將其轉換為生物聚合物或其它產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種有機體從一氧化碳中存活 , 我們用它來分解水 , 產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有許多通路可以被工程代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦在挪威有一個重大的計畫 , 用satoil來捕捉 , 並將油場中的甲烷轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短時間內 , 我覺得會有一種新的領域叫做 「 組合基因組 」 , 因為這些新合成的能力 , 這些廣大的基因組組組合 , 以及同性組合 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 一天可以製造出百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有的生物學 , 透過篩檢 , 不論你在篩檢氫化生產 , 或化學生產 , 或僅僅是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因的角色 , 就會比較好 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 直接從陽光中產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧調節 , 我們有一種氧氣敏感的氧氣 , 我們認為會徹底改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們還在結合纖維 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單的糖和發酵 , 在相同的細胞中 , 產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在使用微生物的大實驗室裡進行 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物化學比我們最好的化學家所產生的複雜度還要多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為 , 未來的工程物種可以是食物的來源 , 希望是能源、環境復甦 , 或許可以取代石化產業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來結束結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在19999年推出實驗的開始 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理評論 , 來評論我們是否應該嘗試並製造一個人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是一項非常奇怪的研究 , 因為各式各樣的宗教領袖用它們的雕塑作為法律書籍 , 他們找不到任何東西 , 禁止製造生命 , 所以 , 最終的關注是生物戰的方面 , 但給了我們啟動這些實驗的原因 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , 史隆基金會剛資助一個多體制的研究 , 來找出對社會的風險和利益 , 以及科學團隊的規則 , 如同我自己在這個領域中使用的 , 我們正試著設立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們能設計東西來產生乾淨能源 , 或許徹底改變發展中國家能做些什麼 , 提供各種簡單的處理方式 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipzimbardo說 , 快樂和成功根源於我們大多數人不認同的特質:我們對過去、現在和未來的看法 。 他建議我們在時代的第一步中展現出外表 , 來改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、幸福、心智、心理學、科學、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo開了一份健康的處方 , 正是時間而已 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的想法 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始時鐘 。 三十秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 。 安頓下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	重點是時間、結束序列 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	十、九、八、七、六、五、四、三、二......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利普辛巴巴巴多:咱們來談談亞當的誘惑 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 拜託 , 不要太清醒了 , 拿一點點吧 。 」 「 我有 。 」
