and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 一直追蹤它的位置 , 讓它可以利用它自己的動作 , 來了解它在環境的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有類似網格的發射模式 , 都有相同的對稱軸 , 相同的格子 , 這裡是橘色的方向 , 這意味著大腦中所有格細胞的net活動應該要根據這六個方向進行改變 , 或在中間的六個方向跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以 , 我們可以把人放到核磁共振掃描儀中 , 讓他們做一個小型電動遊戲 , 就像我給你看的那樣 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你可以在人體皮質裡看到它 , 它也是你在老鼠身上看到的電網細胞的一部分 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車位在距離和方向的位置 , 將建築和界線延伸到他停的位置 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這會是由邊緣偵測細胞的發射來呈現 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從汽車公園走出來的路 , 它會被用來發射網格細胞的路 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種細胞都可以使細胞發射 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他停下來的位置 , 讓他能移動到最好的位置 , 找到在他大腦中的位置細胞的位置模式 , 和他停車的位置模式 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個視覺暗示的位置 , 像是他的車真的在那裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被灌輸了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡找到它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找這種類似網格的發射模式 , 我們會看到一系列的地點 , 當我們做各種自傳記憶任務時 , 比如記得你上次去婚禮時 , 去婚禮 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 代表我們周圍空間的神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重現空間場景 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像它們時發生的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞開始 , 透過這些密集的連結來活化彼此 , 接著 , 反應邊界細胞 , 創造你周圍的景象空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個視角 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 頭部方向細胞 , 我還沒提到 , 它們會像個指南針一樣 , 根據你面臨的方向 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義視覺圖像的方向 , 你可以想像當你在婚禮上發生什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是新時代的一個例子 , 在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理的過程 , 比如你如何記住或想像 , 甚至以數十億個神經元的行為來思考 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 全球安全是由政府、私營部門和大眾所驅動的 。 這不只是開放原始碼粉絲的遙遠期望 , 詹姆士史塔夫斯的願景 , 納粹指揮官的最高階指揮官 , 他們從近期的軍歷史分享vid時刻 , 來解釋為什麼未來的安全應該和橋樑而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放資源、和平政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆士•史塔里斯:nato的最高指揮官認為全球安全性有多大 ?
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要談一些開放資源的安全 , 因為我們必須在21世紀做更好的安全 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	首先讓我說 , 讓我們回顧二十世紀 , 看看安全如何為我們帶來了什麼樣的感覺 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 法國北部的一場戰場 , 位在比利時的北邊 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年的verdun , 在1916年 , 超過300天 , 70萬人被殺害 , 所以一天大約有2 , 000人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它推向第二次世界大戰的20世紀安全 , 你就會看到史達丁格的戰役 , 300天 , 有2百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的後線 , 到第二次世界大戰的黑暗線 , 然後我們進入冷戰 , 鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的論點是 , 與其建造安全牆 , 我們不需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲有名的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	這座橋在大西洋的河邊 , 由ivoandric所組成的小說主題是關於歐洲和巴爾幹部的 , 經過一段時間 , 牆壁是巨大的 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在最近十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始猶豫地團結在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我認為 , 開放的安全是要將國際、國際間、私人公開 , 並將它和戰略溝通結合在一起 , 大多是在社交網路 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我稍微談一下為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物在各種層面下受到攻擊 , 而沒有任何威脅的全球公有物的來源會被建設牆來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	顯然 , 我是個水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一條線 , 穿過印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它沿著它的側邊有凝固電線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	那就是防止海盜攻擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	陰謀是現今全世界非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	陰謀也非常活躍於馬拉卡 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它活躍於幾內亞灣 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到了 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	它是全球交通系統的十億年的不穩定性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 當時有20艘船 , 500艘海底船 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是針對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到另一種海洋 , 網路海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這裡有兩個年輕男性的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	目前 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一份信用卡詐欺 , 將他們淨化超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟的2兆年的連續性 。
two trillion a year .	一年有兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是英國的國內生產總值 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以 , 這個網路海 , 我們無止境地知道是徹底開放的基本原則 , 都在受到威脅的情況下 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	在全球公有物中 , 我擔心的另一件事是人口販賣所造成的威脅 , 由毒品、鴉片、來自阿富汗 , 從歐洲到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心來自安妮海岸的古柯鹼 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器的行動 , 最重要的是 , 也許 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣通常會在海洋中移動 , 但在全球公有物的其他部分 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你們這是我們用來阻止人口販賣的高科技片段 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是一個半導體 , 可以用毒品軟骨來運作 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它被建造在南美叢林裡 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那個低科技的強暴抓住它 , 它帶著六噸的古柯鹼 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個有精密的溝通系統 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種人口販賣 , 在人體、武器、神禁止、大規模毀滅的武器 , 是全球公有物威脅的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	今天我們一起在阿富汗合作 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是在阿富汗的小狗 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上百分之八十到九十的浮木、鴉片和海洛因 , 來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	當然 , 我們也看到恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這就是蓋達組織的所在 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的保險制度 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 這種恐怖主義也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須處理的 。
so here we are , 21st century .	這裡是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道20世紀的工具不會成功 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我認為我們不會直接從槍的桶子裡遞送安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會直接從槍的桶子裡傳送安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這樣做時 , 我們必須做得很好 , 並且有能力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放式安全是關於國際、國際間、私人間的連結 , 由網路上的策略溝通所構成 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子來說明這個方法是如何運作的 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都握有書籍 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 。 我想我讀到這個人口統計 , 年輕的男人和女人在20到30歲 , 大多是在阿富汗 。 」
you would be correct .	你會是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	百分之八十五的百分點是無法讀到阿富汗的安全力量 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班接受教育 , 在這個時期 , 這些男人和女人會學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以 , 問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們教導他們閱讀識字課程 , 由納多和私人機構合作 , 與發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教導了超過二十萬個阿富汗的安全部隊 , 以基本的角度閱讀和寫作 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你讀和寫在阿富汗 , 你通常會把一支筆放在你的口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在典禮上 , 當這些年輕男女畢業時 , 他們用大驕傲的鉛筆 , 把它放在口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這將帶來國際性的50個國家加入這項任務:國際發展機構 , 私人企業 , 採取這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也在教導他們戰鬥技能 , 但我認為 , 開放資源的安全意味著以創造更長久的安全效應的方式連結 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是一個美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘叫 「 憐憫 」 的姐妹船 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院船隻 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這張照片是舒適的 , 在加勒比海和南美洲的海岸進行治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在典型的情況下 , 他們會做四十萬個病人治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它並不是被軍隊制定的 , 而是人道主義組織的結合: 「 希望 」 , 計畫微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織發送義工 。
interagency physicians come out .	內科醫生出來了 。
they're all part of this .	這些都是其中的一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 帶著他的母親走過兩天 , 來到舒適的診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被裝滿時 , 在他的極端靈光眼中 , 他突然抬頭說: 「 媽媽 , veoelmundo 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽 , 我看到世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	將它乘以四十萬個病人治療 , 這種私人合作和安全力量 , 你開始用非常不同的方式創造安全 。
here you see baseball players .	各位可以看到棒球球員 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能選出這張照片中的兩位美國軍人嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是兩位年輕男孩兩邊的年輕男孩 。 這是一系列棒球診所的一部分 , 我們探討主要聯盟棒球、國家部門 , 他們設立外交棒球員 , 他們是真正有技能的士兵 , 但他們參與了這項診所 , 他們在拉丁美洲和加勒比亞、加勒比亞、加勒比亞、加勒比亞、加勒比亞、加勒比亞、加勒比 , 創造了全美洲人 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它展現出年輕男女的榜樣 , 關於健身和生活的典範 , 我主張能為我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	另一方面 , 這種合作關係的另一面是災難的解救 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國的空軍直升機在2004年海嘯攻擊了25萬人 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在每一個重大災難中 , 2004年的海嘯 , 250 , 000人死於巴基斯坦的喀什米里地震 , 2005年 , 8萬5千人死亡 , 海地地震 , 近來大約有30萬人死亡 , 近期 , 日本和其核能產業的結合 , 在所有這些情況下 , 我們看到國際演員的合作關係 , 跨國之間 , 公共事業的關係 , 和安全的關係 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些是開放原始碼安全的例子
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	我們將它綁在一起 , 漸漸地 , 藉由這樣做 。

no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 , 這是推特的圖表 。
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特 。 綠色是地理分配 。
white is the synthesis .	白色是合成 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	它是人口調查的完美演化 , 世界上六大國家 , 下降順序:中國、印度、facebook、美國、推特和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們要拿到這些蚊帳 ?
why do we want to be involved ?	為什麼我們要參與其中 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們先前談到阿拉伯之春的力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉一個例子 , 就是你如何傳遞這個訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦發表了這樣的演講 , 我剛剛說過 , 我在facebook上 , 朋友我 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	聽眾有點笑 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	有一篇文章是ap , 在電線上運行 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	被帶到世界上兩個地方:芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:納粹需要朋友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	故事是種催化劑 , 隔天早上 , 我有數百名facebook朋友的請求 , 來自印尼和芬東 , 大部分都說: 「 miadl , 我們聽說你需要一個朋友 , 喔 , 什麼是nato ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	沒錯 , 我們笑了 , 但這就是我們傳遞訊息的方式 , 傳遞訊息是我們如何連結國際、跨國、私營企業 , 以及這些社交網 , 來協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我用一句話來說明 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是英國士兵的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭守衛中 。
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他站在阿富汗南部的頭盔上 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我把他送來這裡提醒我們 , 我不會希望任何人離開房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力、能創造真正的軍隊效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	那就是我們是誰的核心以及我們所做的事 , 我們去保護自由、言論自由 , 所有我們在社會中珍惜的東西 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但 , 你知道的 , 生命並不是個開關 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要有軍隊 , 要不是更難戰鬥 , 要麼是在敲擊中 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我會說 , 生命是一場風暴 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你必須調整它 , 正如我所想的 , 我們如何在21世紀創造安全 , 將會有時候 , 當我們將真正的權力應用在真實戰爭和危機上 , 但有很多例子 , 如今 , 我們的軍隊可以是創造出21世紀安全、國際安全、跨國、私有的溝通 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後我會說 , 今天早期我們聽說維基百科 , 我常常用維基百科來檢視事實 , 身為你們所有人 , 維基百科並不是由12位聰明的人鎖在房間寫文章所創造的 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	每天 , 維基百科都有成千上萬的人在輸入資訊 , 每天有數百萬人會放棄這些資訊 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	這對根本意義來說 , 沒有人像我們一起思考一樣聰明 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 沒有一個人像我們所有人一樣聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的遠景很簡單:一個每個人都能自由分享的世界 , 在所有知識的總和中 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 透過結合國際間、私人、戰略溝通 , 在21世紀 , 我們可以創造所有安全的總和 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝 。 謝謝 。
